Defense Statement Regarding the Assault on Guo Case 177

Enumerating Four Arguments

Requesting a Decision Not to Prosecute

Regarding the case of Li Cishan, Yin Zhiling, Yang Rongwei, Xie Chengping, Shen Zurong, and others suspected of obstructing official duties in the assault on Guo case, which has already undergone one interrogation, Lawyer Zhao Chen has submitted a defense statement to the Second Special Court, requesting a decision not to prosecute. The reasons for this request are detailed below: (1) Insufficient evidence of criminal suspicion: The assault on Guo Taiqi on May 3rd was purely the act of numerous unknown civilians, and the defendants had absolutely no involvement. There are many pieces of evidence to the contrary, and a few are highlighted below: (1) The four defendants, Li Cishan, Yin Zhiling, Xie Chengping, and Yang Rongwei, representing various groups of the National Salvation United Association, first went to Guo's residence. Shen Zurong, representing the University United Association, then arrived to inquire about the contents of the agreement. During their discussions with Guo Taiqi, no disagreements occurred, and no large crowds of people surged in. Considering the close relationship between the defendants and Guo on ordinary days, they would never resort to violence in either public or private matters. (2) When Guo Taiqi moved to another room to negotiate with the two representatives, Dai Ji and Huang Qiang, the crowd swarmed in, demanding that Guo explain the contents of the agreement. After Guo entered the room, when he leaned on the table and read out the first article of the ceasefire agreement, "Cease all and any combat actions in the vicinity of Shanghai," the crowd misunderstood it to mean that neither the Nanshi nor Pudong areas would be allowed to station troops, and became deeply angered, causing an uproar of accusations. The defendants, Li Cishan and Yin Zhiling, immediately urged the crowd to be patient and listen to the rest of the text. At that time, many in the crowd expressed opposition to Li and Yin, even shouting "Get out, get out!" and hurling abuse at them. This was witnessed and heard by Guo Taiqi himself, which can prove that the defendants never colluded with the crowd in any violent acts. (3) After Guo Taiqi was surrounded by the crowd, the defendants tried in many ways to appease them, but to no avail. Copper coins and teapots were thrown around in a chaotic manner, and the defendants were all in danger of being hit, covering their heads and unable to avoid it. Even if the identities of the perpetrators are unknown, it is undeniable by Guo Taiqi that the defendants did not participate. (4) The only strong evidence for the assault on Guo is Guo himself identifying the perpetrators in court. None of Guo's family members or employees witnessed the event, so their testimonies are unreliable. Since Guo has repeatedly stated to the press that it is difficult to identify the individuals in the crowd at the time, there is essentially no usable evidence in this case, and the defendants should not bear unwarranted responsibility. (5) When the crowd assaulted Guo, there were no fewer than a hundred people. Afterwards, they fled in all directions. If the defendants had participated, why couldn't they have fled with the crowd at that time? Only because of their closer relationship with Guo did they stay at Guo's residence to inquire about his injuries. This is sufficient to presume that the defendants did not inflict any violence on Guo. (6) When the police detectives arrived at Guo's residence, the crowd had already dispersed. The detectives saw that the defendants had not left and suspected them of assault, so they took them to the police station. When Guo heard the news, he was well aware that the two defendants, Li Cishan and Yin Zhiling, were completely innocent. He immediately entrusted Xia Qifeng to personally go to the police station to bail them out. The other defendants were also bailed out by people entrusted by Guo himself. All of this can serve as proof that the defendants are not suspected of committing a crime in this case. Moreover, the defendants are either well-known lawyers in Shanghai, experts in research and education, have studied abroad, or are university professors, all having received higher education. They can argue with reason and defend themselves with facts. How could they resort to such a foolish act of violence? In summary, there is insufficient evidence of criminal suspicion against the defendants, and they should be granted a decision not to prosecute in accordance with Article 244, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law. (2) The act does not constitute a crime: Guo Taiqi was not assaulted while performing his duties according to the law, so Article 142, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law cannot be applied. Based on the circumstances of the day, the assault occurred before he was actually performing his duties. It is presumed that your court believes the defendants are suspected of violating Article 142, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, and is exercising its investigative authority. However, whether a crime is established requires both ordinary and special elements. If one element is missing, a crime is not constituted. The defendants are indeed not suspected of violating Article 142, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Assuming that they are, in addition to the ordinary elements, the following special elements must also be present: 1. Intention to obstruct official duties; 2. Use of violence or coercion; 3. Obstructing the lawful performance of specific duties. However, the defendants did not possess the aforementioned special elements. Furthermore, the duty performed by Guo Taiqi was the signing of the ceasefire agreement, and whether the signing procedure was fundamentally illegal has already become a major issue in national law. Article 27 of the revised Organic Law of the National Government of December 30, 1931, stipulates that "The Legislative Yuan is the highest legislative body of the National Government." "The Legislative Yuan has the power to decide on legislative bills, budget bills, amnesty bills, declarations of war, peace treaties, and other important international matters." In addition, the "Regulations on the Exercise of Sovereignty" passed by the Third Central Executive Committee's Second Plenary Session on June 17, 1929, and promulgated by the National Government on July 3, stipulated in Article 1 that "All legislative bills, financial bills related to the Party's finances, and treaty bills or other international agreement bills related to national rights, which fall within the scope of legislation, may not be established without a resolution by the Legislative Yuan. If they are promulgated and implemented without a resolution by the Legislative Yuan, the Legislative Yuan has the responsibility to raise questions, and the organ that promulgated and implemented them will be deemed to have overstepped its authority. If the Legislative Yuan does not raise questions, it will be deemed to have neglected its duty." According to the above provisions, the Shanghai ceasefire agreement could not be established fundamentally without a resolution by the Legislative Yuan. It is undoubtedly true that it should not have been rashly signed without a resolution by the Legislative Yuan. As a senior diplomat and former acting minister, Guo Taiqi could not claim ignorance of the legal procedures for international agreements to be resolved by the Legislative Yuan, nor could he claim that he was acting on orders from higher authorities and had no choice but to carry them out. Guo also knew that the law has the strongest force and that the power of the law is higher than orders. Performing duties according to the law and performing duties according to orders are clearly strictly distinguished and must not be mistaken. Even though it has already been signed in fact, it is still an illegal signing, and no amount of argument can absolve it of blame. Moreover, it was a signing according to orders, not according to the law, which is an undeniable fact. Taking a step back, even if it is assumed that the defendants are suspected of assaulting Guo, it was obstructing the unlawful performance of a specific duty, not obstructing the lawful performance of a specific duty. The crime of Article 142, Paragraph 2 cannot be established. Even if there was an act of assault, it would at most constitute the crime of "injury out of righteous indignation on the spot" under Article 297 of the Criminal Law. However, according to Article 4 of the "Agreement for the Establishment of Chinese Courts in the French Concession of Shanghai," your court can only investigate cases to which Articles 103 to 186 of the Criminal Law apply. As for other cases, they should be prosecuted by the French Concession authorities or initiated by the victim as a private prosecution. This is assuming that the defendant is suspected of committing a crime. On the one hand, the elements of obstructing official duties according to the law are lacking, and on the other hand, there is no authority to investigate the crime of injury out of righteous indignation. It is already inappropriate to prosecute, let alone when the defendants are inherently free from the suspicion of committing the aforementioned crimes. According to Article [unclear]44, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a decision not to prosecute should be made. (3) The circumstances are minor, and it is more beneficial to decide not to prosecute: The cause of this case stems from the public's patriotic fervor. The public deeply feels the close relationship between national interests and their own interests and is unwilling for the government to take any actions that would cede sovereignty and humiliate the country. The content of the Shanghai ceasefire agreement is controversial, and the public is confused. Guo Taiqi showed people a draft of the agreement in English, so how could the public not misunderstand it? The public, in order to prevent the illegal signing of the ceasefire agreement, took actions outside the bounds of the law. Their public anger was aroused by patriotic zeal, which is forgivable under the law and commendable in spirit. This kind of tragic and intense expression makes outsiders celebrate that the national spirit of China is not to be trifled with and that the patriotic thought is advancing rapidly. It should be cherished and cultivated to nurture a great national spirit, and high-handed measures must not be used to frustrate its lively and vigorous vitality. Remembering that after the Meiji Restoration in Japan, the government worked hard to abolish consular jurisdiction, but various countries set the condition that foreign judges be hired in the courts. At that time, public resentment reached its peak, and when a meeting was held in Hibiya Park, the leg of Foreign Minister Okuma Shigenobu, who was responsible for signing the treaty, was blown off. Also, during the Russo-Japanese War, US President Roosevelt took on the role of mediator. The Japanese government knew that prolonged warfare would likely lead to defeat by Russia, so it seized this opportunity to cease hostilities and negotiate peace, sending its diplomatic representative, Komura Jutaro, to sign the Treaty of Portsmouth. The general public, dissatisfied with the government's humiliating diplomacy, severely beat Komura upon his return to the country. Afterwards, the Japanese government, respecting public opinion, did not pursue the matter in depth. Neither Okuma nor Komura dared to offend public anger, and neither sought prosecution. Furthermore, since the September 18th Incident in the three northeastern provinces last year, Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting was beaten first, followed by National Government Commissioner Cai Yuanpei and Executive Yuan President Chen Mingshu being injured. The central government respected public opinion and did not thoroughly investigate. Wang, Cai, and Chen also did not want to go against public opinion and request the court to severely punish the perpetrators. How is Guo Taiqi's beating any different from the injuries suffered by Okuma, Komura, Wang, Cai, and Chen? At this time, when public misunderstandings have not been resolved and the tide of patriotic anger is at its peak, the handling must be cautious to avoid arousing public indignation. As the saying goes, "Agitation breeds change," and "Preventing the people's mouths is more difficult than preventing a river." It is like a river rising, and if the downstream is blocked, the embankments will collapse, the floods will overflow, and it will be impossible to control. It is necessary to dredge the waterways first so that the flood can flow into the sea, and then the flood will subside. The approach to handling the Guo case is the same. The government does not need to investigate deeply, and the court does not need to severely punish, and then the public anger will subside. Afterwards, they will naturally know to restrain themselves. Moreover, the agreement has already been signed, Guo has not suffered serious injuries, and the circumstances are minor. It is more beneficial to decide not to prosecute, not to mention that the defendants themselves did not commit any violent acts. According to Article 245, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a decision not to prosecute should be made. (4) The victim does not wish for punishment: The victim in this case, Guo Taiqi, has repeatedly stated that he does not wish to investigate deeply. Therefore, he has neither personally filed a private prosecution with the court nor requested your court to prosecute. His intention not to wish for punishment is obvious. According to Article 245, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a decision not to prosecute should be made. Based on the above reasons, I sincerely urge your court to examine the matter closely, weigh the circumstances and the law, and decisively issue a decision not to prosecute, in order to uphold the rule of law and avoid injustice. This would truly be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Procuratorate of the Shanghai Second Special District District Court. (May 24th)

Municipal Health Bureau's Diligent Efforts in Cleaning Up Zhabei 178

Correction of Japanese Newspaper Reports

A letter from the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau to the Shanghai Troop Withdrawal Area Takeover Committee states: With regards, upon investigation, a news report regarding hygiene matters in Zhabei was published in the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun newspaper on the 21st of this month, which is entirely untrue. Furthermore, the Shen Bao and the English-language China Press newspapers also reported that the Director of the Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council reported to the Board of Directors that it was handling part of the street cleaning work in Zhabei, but the wording was ambiguous and should be corrected to avoid confusion. Therefore, the facts are listed below for your Committee to investigate, separately inform, correct, and disclose. (1) On May 21st, the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun newspaper stated that after the Zhabei area was taken over by this city, no preparations had been made for hygiene work. However, when the various parts of Zhabei were occupied by the Japanese army, garbage piled up and urine and feces were scattered everywhere. After the Takeover Committee divided the area and implemented the takeover, the Municipal Health Bureau immediately dispatched street cleaners to carry out work in the areas that had been taken over. Since May 16th, street cleaning has been carried out in the area south of the railway and north of the Suzhou Creek (i.e., part of the jurisdiction of the Fourth District of the Public Security Bureau, as well as the First and Second Sub-offices of the Fourth District) to remove the accumulated garbage and fecal contamination from the Japanese military occupation as the first step. After the accumulated garbage and fecal contamination have been removed, daily street cleaning work will be resumed according to the original method. A total of 160 street cleaners were dispatched, divided into groups to take charge of sweeping, washing, disinfecting, and other tasks, and three administrators were assigned to effectively supervise the work. Since the implementation on the 16th, from the date of takeover to the 20th, more than 8,550 carts of accumulated garbage have been removed, weighing approximately 2,800 tons. It was loaded onto barges and towed by small tugboats to the municipal government's designated landfill at Longhua Wharf for disposal in accordance with the law. In addition, free vaccinations were promoted, and more than 3,800 people have been vaccinated. The above facts can prove that the Japanese newspaper's claim that no preparations were made for hygiene facilities in the areas taken over is completely inaccurate. As for the claim that cholera has occurred in Tanzhiwan, the Municipal Health Bureau had already investigated and confirmed that one person had cholera in Tanzhiwan on April 26th (during the Japanese military occupation before the takeover). However, the patient had been isolated and treated. This further proves that the Municipal Health Bureau is extremely concerned about hygiene and disease prevention and is working hard. The facts should be disclosed to show the reality. (2) On May 21st, the Shen Bao and the English-language China Press newspapers reported that the Director of the Public Health Department of the Public Concession reported to the Chairman of the Board that hygiene work was being carried out in the area around McLaren College and North Sichuan Road on Dixwell Road, and that it seemed that the Chinese authorities would not be able to exercise their powers there for some time. However, that area is still occupied by the Japanese army, and the Takeover Committee has not yet implemented the takeover. However, the Municipal Health Bureau has made full preparations for the rectification of hygiene matters in various parts of Zhabei. Once the takeover is completed, all street cleaning, disinfection, disease prevention, and other work can be implemented immediately. The sooner the Japanese army withdraws, the sooner the hygiene of the residents there can be restored. Looking at the active implementation of hygiene work in the areas that have already been taken over, it can be seen that the Chinese municipal government and the Municipal Health Bureau in charge of this matter attach great importance to and are working hard on this matter.

Investigation After the War in Jiangwan 179

The Chinese Jehol Relief Association believes that it is difficult to ascertain the true situation of the local residents in Jiangwan and other places after the war in Shanghai. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, the Director of the Rescue Team, Zhang Xianqing, led members in a private car to Jiangwan to investigate. The east-west main streets of the town, formerly prosperous markets, had all turned into rubble and rotten wood, a scene of extreme devastation. However, the west main street, Yin Jia Zha, Li Xiaozifang, and nearby shops had not been burned, but bullet holes and gaps were visible everywhere. According to the local people, the descendants of Li Xiaozi were very poor but were able to be self-disciplined and filial, so the neighborhood was also sheltered, and the disaster did not reach them. This shows that good deeds bring blessings, which is credible and substantiated. The Jiangwan Disaster Relief Association for Fellow Villagers has set up a disaster victim registration office inside the Jiangwan Grand Temple Fire Brigade, so that disaster victims can register temporarily and then discuss the situation and provide money and rice. It is heard that there were more than 6,000 shops and residents in the town. Since the Shanghai war, they have all fled to other places. Now that the area is peaceful, the residents are returning home one after another, but they have no homes to return to, and the good disaster victims have no food, clothing, or shelter, making it difficult to survive. In addition to hoping for relief from the government and charitable organizations, countless lives will likely have no way to survive.

Establishment of the Xinwei Relief Association 180

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Urgent Relief of Flood Disasters in Various Provinces and the Shanghai War Zone Refugee Temporary Relief Association have both concluded their work. However, both associations believe that while the disaster was due to fate, it was also caused by human failings. Therefore, in order to learn from past mistakes and prevent future problems, and because nearly 2,000 refugees taken in by the current relief association have no homes to return to, and the relief work in provinces where the urgent relief association has not completed its work still needs to be properly planned for, the association, commemorating the year of the disaster, Xinwei, is named the Xinwei Relief Association and was established yesterday. The charter is recorded below: (Article 1) The purpose of this association is to provide relief to disaster-stricken compatriots in a proactive manner, so that they can each make a living. This association will continue to handle relief matters from the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Urgent Relief of Flood Disasters in Various Provinces and the Shanghai War Zone Refugee Temporary Relief Association in the year Xinwei, hence the name Xinwei Relief Association. (Article 2) This association is initiated and organized by people from various charitable and public welfare organizations in Shanghai. (Article 3) The members of this association will elect 31 directors and 11 supervisors, and the directors will elect among themselves one chairman, one vice-chairman, and nine standing directors to carry out the association's affairs. This association will have an unlimited number of honorary directors. (Article 4) The organization of this association is as follows: Executive Group, Review Group, and Finance Group. Each group will have one director and one deputy director, who will be appointed by the Board of Directors. Organizational regulations and rules of procedure will be drawn up separately. (Article 5) This association may appoint a number of staff members to handle various affairs separately. (Article 6) This association will hold a general meeting of members once a year, a board meeting once a quarter, and a standing board meeting once a month. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. (Article 7) The administrative expenses and operating expenses of this association will be temporarily raised by this association. (Article 8) All income and expenditure of money and goods will be announced in the newspapers at any time. (Article 9) This charter will be reported to the National Government Relief Committee for record after being approved by the General Assembly. (Article 10) If there are any matters not covered in this charter, they may be submitted by the Board of Directors to the General Assembly for amendment. The list of directors includes: Wen Lantong, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Jingren, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Xiaolin, Ye Jingqiu, Huang Hanzhi, Zhao Jinqing, Zhang Xiaoliang, Wang Rutang, Zhu Ziqiao, Wang Yiting, Chen Aishi, Li Zushen, Wu Zhihao, Qu Wenliu, Weng Yinchu, Shen Lisun, Pan Gongzhan, Du Yuesheng, Zhou Shouliang, Huang Bodu, Wang Boqi, Shi Liangcai, Xi Yunsheng, Feng Liutang, Zhou Weishi, Zhang Shenzhi, Gu Jisheng, Guan Yunsheng, Mao Yousheng. The list of supervisors includes: Li Yunshu, Ding Guicen, Lin Kanghou, Huang Jinrong, Yao Wugang, Wu Yunzhai, Gu Xinyi, Zhu Qiluo, Pan Xulun, Xu Yongzuo, Zhu Hujiang. It is said that the joint meeting of directors and supervisors will be held at 4 p.m. today at the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road, where the first joint meeting of directors and supervisors will be held.

Suspension of All Inland Water Launches After the Reopening of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway 181

Temporary Launches to be Completely Removed

Restoration to the Original State Within a Week

After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was interrupted, and inland transportation relied entirely on launches. The number of temporary launches on the Shanghai-Suzhou route greatly increased. Now that the Beijing-Shanghai Railway has begun to operate, a large number of inland water vessels can only suspend their operations. The recent situation is recorded below.

Early Morning Launches to Shanghai-Suzhou 182

On the Shanghai-Suzhou route, only China Merchants and Yuan Tong had ships operating. When the January 28th Incident occurred, a large number of refugees from Shanghai fled to Suzhou and Changzhou, and the Shanghai-Zhang Company and others temporarily added early morning launches, traveling back and forth daily to avoid the dangers of night航. After the [unclear] Incident, others followed suit, and there were China Merchants, Yuan Tong, Qingji, Heping, Yongyuan, Shanghai-Zhang, Zhengchang, Tongji, and Central companies, each forming a single early morning launch to Shanghai-Suzhou, specializing in carrying passengers. Freight, postal items, and newspapers were carried by mid- and late-day launches. In addition, the Changzhou-Xichang-Ganlu launches also sailed to Suzhou. The development of the Shanghai-Suzhou ships was unprecedented.

Suspension Due to Few Passengers 183

Recently, the number of inland water launches has increased daily, while the number of passengers has decreased daily. The launch companies, competing for business, have reduced ticket prices. A first-class cabin, which sold for 48 yuan during the war, has now fallen to 12 yuan, and still no one is chartering it. A deck seat has also fallen to 1.10 yuan. Recently, each launch has only made a little more than 100 yuan per trip, which is not enough to cover the cost of coal, food, and other expenses. Yesterday, when the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was opened, the number of passengers decreased sharply. Each morning at the Old Gate Bridge, the barkers from each company had no passengers to solicit. Although they have not completely disappeared, there are only a few. The launch companies are currently discussing suspending operations.

Restoration to the Original State 184

It was heard yesterday that the China Merchants and Yuan Tong companies in the Shanghai-Suzhou launch route have decided that if no one boards the early morning launches, they will restore the Shanghai-Suzhou night launches, specializing in carrying cargo, and will restore the alternating daily service between the two companies. The temporary launches that were opened during the war, which have no fixed routes, will also have to be suspended, and each will open its original routes. It is planned to return to the situation before the January 28th Incident in one week. China Merchants will send newly built launches to operate on the Suzhou route.

Suzhou Customs Revenue 185

Since the outbreak of the war, the affairs of Suzhou Customs have greatly increased, and the tax revenue has also greatly increased. Originally, the tax revenue of Suzhou Customs relied entirely on one or two Shanghai ships, and the monthly income was barely enough to cover the salaries of the customs officers. After February, the number of launches greatly increased, and the tax revenue also improved. Now that the ships are about to suspend operations, the tax revenue of Suzhou Customs will plummet again.

Proposal for Summarizing Accounts at the End of June 186

After the outbreak of the January 28th War, the period for summarizing accounts for the 20th year of the Republic of China by the business community was agreed to be held at the end of May. Now that it is approaching, a part of the merchants in this city, according to the usual practice of Shanghai banks, propose that the settlement of accounts for this time of the business community can be held in accordance with the end of June, so that the transfer of accounts, interest, settlement, and other items will be consistent with the annual settlement of the banks, which will be convenient for all industries. They have petitioned the central government and the municipal chamber of commerce.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Requesting Collection of Taxes Based on Actual Rent 187

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Secretary-General of the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: With regards, it has been approved that the First District Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Federation has sent a letter stating that, according to the representatives of the Zhenbo Church, Wu Huichuan, Xie Senchang, Liu Zhongfa, Shunxingxiang, Xi Shengsen, Gutai Chang, Gu Fangsheng, and Zhou Rongzhang, Zhou Yiqing, and Lu Yinhua of Zhili Road, the rent for each room in Zhili Road is 32 yuan per month, and the police tax has also been calculated according to the rent over the years. However, at about 3 p.m. today, a Western employee of the Municipal Council came to collect the police tax, forcibly wanting to calculate the rent for each room as 40 yuan. The representatives believed that the police tax was based on the amount of rent, and there was an old precedent to follow, but the employee forcibly wanted to increase the tax and threatened that if the tax was not calculated according to the 40 yuan rent and sent to the tax office, the police would seal the door in three days, and copied down the door numbers. The representatives were therefore extremely alarmed and begged the association to forward the employee's coercive tax increase and threats to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association to uphold justice. According to this, the Municipal Council forcibly estimates high rent prices in order to increase its revenue, directly causing tenants to bear an additional burden and indirectly promoting opportunities for landlords to raise prices. Such actions that oppress the common people are not what the Municipal Council, which is responsible for ensuring the safety of residents and maintaining local order, should do, nor can they be done by public officials. Similar cases have been repeatedly disputed by your association in the past. Now that we have received the above report, we should forward it for review, and we sincerely hope that you will negotiate with the Municipal Council as soon as possible to show fairness and protect the residents. It is inappropriate to collect taxes based on estimates that do not correspond to actual rents. Your office has repeatedly corrected this, but the tax office of your bureau has repeatedly and deliberately violated this, not knowing what the intention is. In the four reasons stated in your bureau's recent reports, except for one that is natural, the second, whether the house certificate has the word "Yi" on it, the third is purely speculation rather than fact, and the fourth should be handled according to the law if there is concrete evidence. This association believes that the financial plan of your bureau's treasurer is admirable, but it does not consider the method of actually adding to the tax to be bright, and it is actually against economic principles and property rules. The letter is hereby forwarded, and we hope that you will investigate and quickly order corrections so that you will not try again and cause more disputes.

Notice of Proposed Water and Electricity Price Increase in the French Concession 188

Property Owners' Association Objects

The issue of water price increases in the International Settlement remains unresolved, and there are also rumors of increases in water and electricity rates in the French Concession. According to insiders, water and electricity prices in the French Concession are already relatively high compared to other areas. Therefore, there is no justification for further price increases. Moreover, the number of residents in the French Concession has been increasing year by year, and the water company's income has doubled, resulting in substantial profits. However, the company is now citing large expenses as a reason to request the Municipal Council to increase both water and electricity rates uniformly. The Municipal Council is currently considering the request and has not yet approved it. The Shanghai Property Owners' Association is greatly concerned upon hearing this news, believing that water and electricity rates in the French Concession are already higher than those in other areas, and further increases would only burden residents. They plan to send a letter to the French Concession Municipal Council, urging the Chinese directors to pay close attention and find ways to thwart the company's price increase plan.

Japanese Morphine Operation Busted on West Jiaxing Road 191

Japanese National Nakamura Arrested on the Spot

Morphine worth 35,000 gold coins Seized

A Japanese national named Nakamura had been secretly operating an illegal morphine sales operation at No. 18, Sande Lane, West Jiaxing Road, Hongkou. After the Municipal Council regained police authority in the Hongkou district, it resolved to severely crack down on such illegal operations. Wang Changgen and Zhao Bingkun, Chinese detectives of the Chief Inspector's Office of the General Inspectorate, reported the recent activities of the Japanese national to the authorities. A search warrant was requested from the First Special District Court, ordering Song Bingzheng, an investigator specializing in the prohibition of narcotics, and Pan Gensi, the western detective, to proceed to the address to conduct a search. The house was in a Japanese style. The Japanese national Nakamura resided on the upper floor, while the rear building and the pavilion were equipped with machines for manufacturing narcotics, with morphine stored inside. The Chinese and Western detectives, having previously obtained a search warrant from the Japanese consulate, immediately entered the premises and began the search. In addition to seizing narcotics on the spot, they also arrested nine Chinese residents in the house: Fang Yinbao, Lin Huiqing, Zhou Yongyuan, Yang Xiuwen, Guo Yuming, Chen Ruikang, Wang Kaiyan, Su Ahui, and Diao Jintang. The Japanese national Nakamura was also handed over by the detectives to the Japanese police officers who accompanied them to the Japanese Consulate. Yesterday morning, Fang and the other eight were sent to the First Special Court, where Magistrate Qiao Wanxuan conducted a preliminary hearing. According to Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, the defendants were being prosecuted under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law because they possessed substitutes for opium with the intention of selling them. It is reported that 119 pounds of morphine powder were seized, estimated to be worth over 35,000 gold coins, and all kinds of machinery are temporarily stored in the police station. As for the Japanese national Nakamura, a separate lawsuit will be filed with the relevant consulate. The Chinese and Western detectives then reported the circumstances of the search of the house. Magistrate Qiao then interrogated Fang Yinbao and the others one by one. The defendants all claimed that the drugs found were actually insecticide. As a result, the defendants were still detained pending further questioning. It is also reported that Magistrate Qiao will schedule a personal inspection of the house at a later date in order to gain a clear understanding of the situation for reference.

French Concession Security Gun Donation Company Case Opens 192

Sixteen Households Already Registered and Paid

Mao Jingeng and Mao Jinsheng, head detectives of the French Concession's McLane Police Station, along with deputy detectives Wang Rusong and Jiang Changwen, and patrol detectives Gu Mingzhou and Lu Jinxiang, raided the Security (Gun Donation) Company at No. 8, Building B, Public Concession Road at noon the day before yesterday. They arrested Zhang Shengfu, a Ningbo native who was the accountant, and fourteen employees: Zhang Debao, Song Bolin, Yu Xueming, Yu Gansheng, Wang Kailiang, Shi Guifu, Lu Aquan, Du Arong, Chen Baorong, Han Huangjin, Zhou Lansheng, Wang Guihua, and Wang Hengchun. The main culprit is still at large. Fifteen people who were waiting to register, including Shen Jifu, Lu Meiqing, Han Aquan, Gong Yimin, Feng Yongfu, Gu Chengfa, Xu Yongning, Zhao Shiquan, Hong Achun, Zhang Genfu, and Liu Jiacai, were also taken to the police station. Subsequently, the police found that sixteen households had already registered and paid donations, including Xu Zhaoming, upstairs at Yufu Barber Shop, No. 87 Jixiang Street, who donated three opium pipes; Sun Yongchang, upstairs at Dingji Barber Shop, Xizilaihuo Street entrance of Fadamalu Road, who donated four opium pipes; Shangyushe, No. 82, Caishi Street entrance of Zhengjia Muqiao Street, who donated five opium pipes; Gao Jinsheng, No. 963, Xujiahui Road intersection of Bedang Road, who donated six opium pipes; Liu Sangji, No. 97, Baxianfang, who donated seven opium pipes; Sun Atang, No. 7, Lanfang Lane, Caishi Street, who donated nine opium pipes; Le Gongyu, No. 2, Tianxi Lane, Zhengjia Muqiao, who donated eight opium pipes; Chen Gengang, No. 331, Aiduya Road, who donated ten opium pipes; Daguangming, No. 67, Baoyu Lane, who donated fourteen opium pipes; Xu Asan, No. 25, Deshan Lane, who donated fourteen opium pipes; Zhao Shiqi, Wan Shangseng, Chen Asheng, Zhang Shaoji, Ni Xiangxian, and Zheng Yinlu, each donated one opium pipe, waiting for business. At 3:00 PM, Magistrate Zhang Chaozuo and Clerk Wang Yihui arrived at the First Criminal Court for trial. According to Fei Xizhen, the police lawyer, the police temporarily charged the defendants with joint fraud and obtaining property under Article 363 of the Criminal Law. As the main culprit is currently at large and the police procedures are not yet complete, a postponement was requested pending further investigation and apprehension of the main culprit. Patrol Detective Gu Mingzhou reported the details of the bust, presenting the evidence. He stated that he had selected thirteen or fourteen of the defendants, who claimed that the company had hired them as bodyguards and entrusted them with buying six pistols, priced at 330 yuan, with a deposit of 200 yuan paid in advance. When questioned, the defendant Zhang Shengfu stated that he had been hired as an accountant by a friend and had only been there for one day, unaware of the details. The other thirteen defendants all stated that they were either tea servers or shop assistants, and some had not yet been assigned duties. After the interrogation, the court ordered Shen Jifu and the other fifteen to appear in court to be questioned one by one about their registration. The court then announced that the hearing would be adjourned to May 31 for further investigation, and the defendants were temporarily detained in the police station, while Shen Jifu and the others were dismissed pending further notice.

Amicable Settlement Reached in the Bitter Jade Lawsuit Involving the Gongfa Company 193

The bitter jade lawsuit in the bankruptcy case of Shanghai Riyue Bank's Gongfa Company, previously filed with the Second Special Court by Liu Baogeng, represented by lawyers Lin Yingqing, against liquidators accountant Pan Zhaobang, Wu Zheng, and Huang Xianzhong, son of Huang Chujiu, seeking joint ownership of the jade, was ruled in favor of Liu Baogeng. Subsequently, the accountants and others, dissatisfied with the original judgment, appealed to the Higher Third Branch Court. A settlement was reached in court before Justice Zhao Zhenhai and clerk Yin Tingxiang. The main points of the settlement are as follows: (1) Appellant Liu Baogeng agreed to abandon his claim of joint ownership of the jade, and the appellants were responsible for seeking the consent of the creditor group that had previously sued the Gongfa Company to repay the appellant 2,700 yuan for washing, cutting, and transportation expenses as a final settlement. The unfinished incense burner, jade waist section, and fourteen pieces of material were to be claimed from the original court by the appellant in the name of Baohua Xiang Firm, and entrusted to Yizhen Le for the continuation of the full washing and cutting project within a period of two years. 35% of the sale price of the future finished product will be allocated as wages and all expenses for the appellant to continue the work. Both parties agreed that the settlement was established. (2) The litigation costs of both trials shall be borne equally by both parties.

Changes in the Hardoon Estate Case 194

The Estate is Valued at Over 20 Million Yuan

Samuel No Longer Represents the Plaintiff

According to the Continental News, the estate of Jewish tycoon Hardoon is valued at over 20 million yuan. When Hardoon died, his will was entirely held by his wife. Sir Glynn also ordered Islah Hardoon to deposit litigation costs in advance to prevent defeat before the case could proceed. Academia Sinica's New Invention in the Research of Domestic Wine Qu 197

Dr. Zeng Yi, who was previously sent by the Academia Sinica to Sichuan Province to investigate tung oil and discovered the ruins of an ancient volcano, recognized that China's wine imports exceed 6 million taels of silver annually, with Eastern imports accounting for half of that amount. Moreover, domestically produced wine, made using traditional methods, is worth tens of millions of taels of silver annually, but the traditional methods result in low production and cannot compete with foreign wines and alcohol. Furthermore, domestic wine merchants are currently purchasing foreign spirits to mix with drinking wine, which is harmful to health. Therefore, there is a need for research and improvement. Dr. Zeng returned to the Chemical Research Institute of the Academia Sinica to research domestic wine qu. Recently, he extracted several fermentation microbes from wine qu produced in northern China. The wine-making ability of one of these microbes has now been successfully tested. From now on, China's old wine-making methods can be fundamentally scientificized through the success of this experiment. In the future, China's wine-making qu can be completely replaced with a small amount of "Cai bacteria" (named by Dr. Zeng as Cai bacteria in honor of President Cai Yuanpei, who strongly advocated scientific research at the institute). However, the yield is 25% higher than the highest yield obtained from Chinese distilleries. It is reported that the method for producing "Cai bacteria" is extremely convenient. Previously, the production of Chinese wine qu involved many superstitious taboos and took a month. Now, according to Dr. Zeng's new method, it only takes three days. Rice and wheat flour can be used as raw materials, and an artificial incubator or a low-temperature thermostat can be used as equipment. Dr. Zeng is now producing this bacteria on paper, similar to silkworm seed paper, or sealing it in glass tubes for easy mailing, and plans to open a factory in the future to sell it worldwide. It is also reported that the wine-making ability of this "Cai bacteria" is unprecedented and has never been recorded abroad. Previously, Keermaiti of the Pasteur Institute in France extracted a microbe from Annam wine qu with a maximum wine-making power of only 3.5%, while Dr. Zeng's pure "Cai bacteria" can produce more than 20% alcohol, a difference like heaven and earth, and a new contribution to the international academic community. Dr. Zeng's wife, Ms. Hu Ze, who holds a bachelor's degree, also researches wine qu with Dr. Zeng at the institute and discovered a yellow microbe. Its wine-making ability is slightly inferior to "Cai bacteria," but the wine tastes quite good. As there is no name for this bacteria in China, it is proposed to be named "Yang bacteria" to commemorate Mr. Yang Xingfo, who strongly advocated scientific research in China. It is reported that the qu bacteria used in Japanese sake and Chinese Shaoxing wine are of the same family as "Yang bacteria."

Three Kidnappers Executed 198

Execution of Kidnappers of Women and Children

Shen Asan, a kidnapper from Wuxi, 20 years old, and Yu Zhulin, a kidnapper from Ningbo, 34 years old, used firearms to organize a gang on November 7 of last year, broke into Jiang Zirong's iron shop on Tiantong Road, kidnapped Jiang's seven-year-old son and family, hid them at No. 15 Huishan Road, and demanded a ransom of 50,000 yuan. The case was discovered, and the detectives of the Huishan Police Station arrested them and sent them to the First Special District Court. After interrogation and clear confession, Shen and Yu were each sentenced to death. Another kidnapper, Jiang Dinghui from Yangzhou, 24 years old, organized a gang on January 10 of this year, kidnapped the widow Wang Yu from No. 71 Taian Lane, North Shaanxi Road, and demanded a ransom. He was arrested by the Huishi Police Station and sent to the Special District Court, where he was sentenced to death and sent to prison for verification. Now, the Special Court has reported the files of the above two cases to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for verification and execution. Yesterday morning was the deadline, and the police sent Shen, Yu, and Jiang to the First Special Court one after another. Magistrate Shen declared to the three criminals that today was the day of execution by firing squad and asked if they had any last words or to notify their families. According to Shen Asan, please send a letter to his brother-in-law Zhang Yaokui at Beimentang, Wuxi, to come to Shanghai to collect his body. Yu Zhulin said he had no last words, but only asked to use the eight yuan found on his person to buy a pair of shoes and socks and two pieces of tin foil. Jiang Dinghui said, please send a letter to Yan Huaiyu at No. 305 Aiwenyi Road, asking him to come and collect his body, and had nothing else to say. He also requested food and wine. Magistrate Shen ordered them to be sent to the local court for execution. The Chinese and Western police then took the three criminals down, along with the files and photos, and escorted them in a prisoner car to the Caohejing execution ground. They also notified the local court, and the prosecutor supervised the execution and verified the identity of the criminals before carrying out the execution by firing squad.

Headless Male Corpse in Suzhou Creek 199

Neck Cut Very Clean

A headless male corpse floated to the bank of Suzhou Creek near the Xinzha Bridge yesterday morning. Wall of Former Tianchan Stage Collapses Late at Night 200

Fortunately No One Injured Due to Late Hour

Trams on All Routes Detour

The site of the former Tianyi Stage theater on Nanjing Road, between Zhejiang Road and Hubei Road, has been in disrepair for some time. The owner hired workers to dismantle and rebuild it. The site was surrounded by bamboo fences, and the roof had been gradually dismantled, but the four walls were still standing. However, having lost the support, and exposed to the erosion of wind and rain, the walls were in a dangerous state. Suddenly, at around 3:00 AM yesterday, the wall along Hubei Road collapsed with a loud crash, and bricks and stones fell, mixed with mud. Fortunately, it was late at night, and there were no pedestrians or vehicles, so no one was injured. If this had happened during the day, the area, which is usually a busy traffic area, would have suffered serious damage. After the wall collapsed, bricks and stones piled up on the road. It was not possible to clear them at night, so the Public Works Department sent workers to clear them at dawn. Trams on routes 3, 5, and 6 had to pass through the area. Yesterday, due to the obstruction, trams traveling south from the north turned east at the Wulong Risheng Building on Zhejiang Road, and trams traveling north from the south turned east at the Wuma Road intersection and traveled along the Bund to Nanjing Road. Although this was a slight detour, traffic was not inconvenienced. By the afternoon, the remaining bricks and rubble on the road had been completely cleared.

He Shousun 201

Requests Divorce from Husband

Married for Thirteen Years Without Children

Husband Abandons Her; She Requests Divorce

He Shousun, a female employee of the Municipal Education Bureau, is currently 37 years old and originally from Jiangxi. In 1920, when Ms. He was 24 years old, she was engaged to Liu Shicheng, a fellow villager, through her parents' arrangement. However, although they have been married for thirteen years, they have had no children due to Liu's hidden illness. In addition, the relationship between the couple is extremely poor, and their interests are completely opposed. For the sake of her future happiness, Ms. He has hired lawyer Shi Lin to petition the First Special District Court for divorce mediation. However, because the conditions proposed by Liu are difficult to accept, the mediation has been unsuccessful. She is now formally filing for divorce against Liu. The petition states that she became engaged to Liu in 1920 and was originally scheduled to marry the following winter. However, Liu suddenly requested a postponement. By February 1922, he deliberately violated customs and insisted on returning to their original hometown of Ganzhou to marry. After the marriage, he was arrogant towards the plaintiff because he disliked the plaintiff's family's poverty. His temperament was also eccentric, and he often scolded and quarreled. The plaintiff tolerated him as much as possible, so she was often silent. During the summer vacation of 1925, the plaintiff wanted to return to Nanchang to visit her father and notified the defendant before departure, agreeing to go together. However, he was slow to act, which clearly showed his wealth and unwillingness to live with the plaintiff. In 1931, the defendant held a position in the Secretariat of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, earning a substantial income. He often took leave to come to Shanghai, but always stayed elsewhere, unwilling to see the plaintiff. Even if he visited, he would avoid her, as if she was a stranger. There was no affection to speak of. It was found that the defendant had been diagnosed by a doctor eight years ago as having physiological changes that made it difficult to have children. Therefore, although the plaintiff had conceived once, the fetus died in the womb. Although the doctor removed the corpse by surgery, the position of her waist and abdominal muscles has been distorted ever since, and she has had no children to this day. This is really affected by the defendant's chronic disease. For the sake of descendants, for the sake of family happiness, and to avoid the pain of both parties, she specifically applied for mediation. However, when the court held a mediation hearing on April 23, the defendant did not appear in court. His lawyer instead asked the plaintiff to continue to live with him and bear the responsibility of support, resulting in unsuccessful mediation. As the defendant suffers from an incurable disease and has abandoned her, she requests that a divorce be granted. Magistrate Yang of the First Special Court opened a hearing yesterday morning. The defendant, Liu Shicheng, is currently employed at the Hangyuan Telegraph Bureau. After receiving the summons, he immediately came to Shanghai and surrendered to the court with his representative lawyer. Magistrate Yang then questioned them, stating that both parties were intellectuals and had been married for many years. They should live together for a long time, and why should they rush to divorce? He advised both parties to go outside and conduct a settlement. The case was adjourned for further hearing.

According to Mr. Zhang's ambition, China's technology sector should organize a large-scale group, hire interpreters proficient in various foreign languages, and go to European and American countries to promote China's national skills. This would not only absorb foreign money but also win glory for the country, so that it would no longer be despised by foreigners and laughed at as the "Sick Man of East Asia." It is reported that the programs that Mr. Zhang and his entire class will perform at Summer Peak tomorrow are all skills honed over 20 years, with divine courage and agility, making people speechless. It is expected that those who go to watch will be crowded.

Free Talk

Quotations from the Ninety-Three-Year-Old Ma Xiangbo

A Simple Explanation of Acquiring Knowledge 208

— Lai Zha

Throughout my life, I have always enjoyed reading philosophy because philosophy is the key to studying all sciences. I translate philosophy as "the study of acquiring knowledge" because only with "acquiring knowledge" can one then "investigate things." Only with logic can one then begin to research.

The more I read philosophy, the more interested I became. I lit Western candles at night and read late into the night, until my eyesight became nearsighted.

At that time, buying books was really difficult. Ships from Europe had to go around the Cape of Good Hope, making a large circle. Writing a letter to order a book would take one or two years to get a reply. Later, the Suez Canal opened (Editor's note: The Suez Canal opened in 1869), and ships could pass through the canal, pulled by horses on the shore, making transportation more convenient.

I believe that the best philosophical works are in Latin. I once compiled a textbook for Aurora University called "A Simple Explanation of Acquiring Knowledge." Later, I revised it and had it published by the Commercial Press. This "Simple Explanation of Acquiring Knowledge" was compiled based on several of the most basic Latin writers. In my translation of various terms, I often used Buddhist and Taoist terminology. For example, "Individu" is usually translated as "individual," but I translated it as "juziti" [局自體, roughly "self-contained entity"], which is a term from Buddhist scriptures. For example, the space occupied by volume, I called "fangwei" [方位, "location"], which is also a term from Buddhist scriptures.

"A Simple Explanation of Acquiring Knowledge" only covers the section on terminology. However, reading this book will reveal the shortcomings of the Chinese language.

Humorous Tales from the Wisteria Pavilion 209

— Songlu

Since the assassination of Japan's Inukai Cabinet, the military's arrogance has been rampant. Fascism is rising to a fever pitch. The party cabinet is on the verge of collapse. Indeed. News arrived that the "Wood Cabinet" (Suzuki) disappeared. The "Wisteria Cabinet" (Saito) rose. It is seen that from now on, Japanese militarists will gain power, and party politics will hang by a thread. As the "Wisteria Cabinet" is just beginning its tenure, I will express my humble views as humorous tales.

The wisteria, as a material, is both firm and strong, possessing both hardness and softness. Japan's foreign policy has always combined threats and enticements. It is said to be good at using both its soft and hard strengths. From now on, Saito's administration will increasingly show its old wisteria bark face, pulling and dragging.

Wisteria is a plant that lives by climbing on trees. This time, Saito's cabinet is "wisteria" in name, and he is only following the lead of Araki's "wood". This is also expected.

Some may say, Suzuki is also "wood." Why did it yield to wisteria? I say, Suzuki's wood, although not rotten wood, is only wood tied to a bell. It is ultimately not a great vessel. Therefore, it is not enough to support a large building, unlike the strong fruit of old wisteria.

Others ask me, If we discuss the meaning of the name "Saito Cabinet," can we also infer its policies? I say, Wisteria, as a material, wraps around every gap. If one tree is not enough, it goes to another. It is the most aggressive of plants. The policies of the Wisteria Cabinet may be just like that. Japanese officials with "wisteria" in their names are seen in the newspapers, such as Sato, Kato, and Ito. Now, Saito is added, shining together, and the Japanese cabinet can be considered a wisteria ware shop.

Mr. Chan-jia read the meaning of my article and laughed, Wisteria is not only for making canes and weaving yellow wisteria objects. There is also loofah vine for loofah, watermelon vine for watermelon, prickly hair vine for stinging people, and wolfberry vine for making dishes.

I say, That's right. This is truly "a dog dies, then wisteria". "Inu" (dog) died and Saito succeeded. What else could it be if not "a dog dies, then wisteria"? Those who heard it all applauded.

Candle Shadows Flickering Red (Sending Miss Su's Coffin for Burial on February 21st) 210

(It has not been two months since Lingxi returned to his hometown. Looking at Jiyuan and his maternal grandfather's old residence from the boat, he felt sad and wanted to cry.)

At dawn, the stream rushes. For whom are the oarsmen urging in the wind? The flowers on the shore and the red sun are irresistibly beautiful, just illuminating the eyebrows of people. Fleeting years pass quickly, exchanged for a jade coffin poured eastward by turbulent waves. The fragrant soul fondly remembers the ink-wash homeland. The white-haired subject of Du Fu. The daytime horn sounds from the river sky. End the war-torn alarm; the cuckoo cries bitterly. The weeds in the mortuary do not become spring. Remembering Prince Wang's road of death. Wearing white linen like snow, the twilight approaches. Arriving at the river bridge, how desolate to complain. Enduring long-term regrets, transform into a round ice. Deep at night, illuminate you.

Slow Tune of the Long Pavilion 211

(Remembering Miss Su when the car passed Bansong Garden; she wanted to visit when she was in Shanghai but never did.)

Again, the dream car dust is blown up. The painted garden pavilions, heartbreaking to see. The mirror railing, spring waves, I wanted to arrive then but never did. The smoke-dried peach blossoms dye the willows, replacing the taste of sorrow. Tearful eyes look at the orioles, asking if there are flower-front bells and pendants. The porter sighs at the graceful shadows, buried in the singing of five sighs. Wildly joyous Shanghai city, letting go of the watery weather. The remaining lonely swallows in the east wind argue about returning to the tortoiseshell beam. Counting the drunken eyes and lamp lips, everything is avoided for her sake.

A Scene from Military Life 212

— Hanlu

On the day of visiting the troops in Kunshan and Taicang, the sound of sentry gunfire could be heard continuously. Although the situation was very serious, all the officers and soldiers were calm and happy. There was absolutely no sense of the terror of war.

A gentle breeze wafted the melodious sound of a record, faintly discernible as a section from the Cantonese opera "Willow Shakes Gold." In the trenches, one could often see a special kind of military equipment: gramophones. This was indeed their only source of entertainment.

On the exercise ground under Ma'an Mountain, many armed comrades were working hard in a football competition. The referee was a young officer. His interest was as strong as in school life. Others, engaged in national martial arts performances and martial arts competitions, showed even greater courage and exuberance.

A small team of soldiers was seriously engaged in "crossing the river" exercises. On the riverbank, they took off their military uniforms and pants, raised their pistols and rifles, and waded through the cold, muddy river, shouting and struggling. When they reached the shore, everyone was very excited and did not even mind their muscles turning red from the cold.

Battalion Commander Shen, who was leading the tour, gave us a brief explanation. He said, "We firmly believe that in order to strengthen combat capabilities, spiritual strength is more important than material things. Our military training method focuses on the realization of the 'militarization of the military' and aims to make the brothers' lives happy, lively, and interesting. Therefore, in addition to daily exercises, the promotion of various entertainment activities has gradually become a regular routine."

I could not help but admire the Nineteenth Route Army's perfect organization and great spirit. At the same time, associating the military entertainment with a recent audio-visual national film "Silver Star Luck," which combined various songs and games, gave me spiritual pleasure. The "Victory Gong and Drum," among other things, hinted at the deep meaning of saving the country. It can be seen that in times of national crisis, there is no need to abandon proper entertainment.

On the vast return journey, a scene from military life kept appearing. Also thinking, mental consolation to the soldiers, "Silver Star Luck" is indeed a good contribution. However, it is best to drink heartily on the day of capturing Huanglong [the enemy's capital].

Americans Plan to Visit the Moon Palace 213

— Yinhong

Recently, in Ohio, USA, a young engineer named Woodfud is engaged in manufacturing a rocket that flies seven miles per second. He intends to use this for traveling to the moon. He claims that he can reach the moon in 200 hours.

Upon investigation, Mr. Wood is not the first American to dream of visiting the Moon Palace. Several years ago, a man named Cookhtan approached the famous astronomer Camille Klamarion with the same plan, inviting him to be a travel companion. Mr. Klamarion's reply was quite humorous, saying that he could not leave his post, but if the brave warrior made a second trip, he would definitely accompany him.

Mr. Cookhtan also put aside his original plan. It was probably because Mr. Klamarion did not agree to go with him.

Interview with Mrs. Gandhi (Part Two) 214

— Huang Yingdai

"Have you ever seen these things with your own eyes?" I asked.

As we were discussing this issue, suddenly a deafening sound came, drumming, cymbals, and bells, sent from the temple across the street. These girls shouted in unison:

"What cruel actions these are!"

"Have you met Mr. Gandhi recently? What do you think of him?" I asked.

"He said he was fine, but I said to him, 'Why do I only see your bones?' But he said he must feel fine."

"But he said his diet has now changed. He no longer eats sheep's milk but eats raisins and fruit juice."

"What did he think after Miss Slade was arrested?" I asked.

"I told him that they had taken Mirabehn away, but he said, 'Yes, they have taken her away.' He had already known about this."

"He knew everything. He had told me before that she was going to be arrested, and everything he predicted would come true."

"What exactly happened to those cruel things?" the young man shouted. At that time, the noise from across the street seemed even more intense. Crackle, crackle, like thunder in a rainstorm.

"What are your plans now, Madam?" I asked. "Do you want to go back to prison and be a prisoner again?"

"My plan is to continue working for the motherland," she replied. "Serving for the motherland, everything is left to God's disposal. We"

"Should be patient, and I am preparing for something unfortunate to happen!"

Mrs. Gandhi stood up, gave the Indian farewell greeting, and shook hands with me. At the same time, the young man refused to deny it, insisting that those cruel events had happened again.

"Okay, so what exactly happened?" I asked him, and it was the first time I had spoken to him.

He stared at me intently for a while.

"Have you seen those things?" I asked.

"No."

"Then, personally, do you know anyone who does these things?"

"No."

"Child," I said, "there is only one rule here. No matter what, I cannot believe anything to be true that I have not seen."

"So what is this then?" he shouted.

"Wind," was my answer. At the same time, I bowed and left.

Record of Double Towers in Military Life (62) 215

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Eight: Boundless Sorrow and Resentment in Repentance; It's Difficult to Hope for Open-Mindedness; Extreme Singing and Dancing; Enjoyment Reveals Authority

Sure enough, with just this little bit of something, you won her true heart's delight, and she was extremely willing to help you vigorously. On the spot, she invited Military Governor Ye to come, and she agreed in person. Your matter can be considered nine and nine-tenths complete. There is also a person named Mao Deshun, who is the youngest son of Mao, the music teacher who used to play the huqin and teach opera. He often followed his father to serve in our hall. He used to play the yueqin. Now that he has grown up, he has joined Fifth Madam's place. He has been promoted and changed his profession to become Fifth Madam's personal adjutant. When I saw him, I also gave him some money, because I heard that Military Governor Ye is very difficult to meet. You can't compare to me being able to enter and exit the halls and rooms at will. Go directly to Fifth Madam to find a way. In the future, if you go to see Old Ye alone, you may inevitably encounter obstacles. Then you can use this little Mao to find an opportunity to lead you in. Most likely, little Mao will arrange everything properly in half a day and personally invite you. You only need to prepare how you should speak when you see Old Ye. Make sure that what you say is in tune with him, and then you can achieve the greatest purpose. An Yutian hurriedly smiled and said, "You are really capable. I don't understand any of these ways. If it weren't for you helping me, I wouldn't have even dreamed of doing this. I will have to trouble you to teach me often in the future." Liang Xiaoyun smiled triumphantly and silently pondered. Then she thought of many questions, and gradually brought them up one by one for detailed discussion with An Yutian, and to study the future position and the ultimate hope. An Yutian thought that his qualifications were shallow and his influence was small, and that his requests should not be too extravagant. If he could get a leisurely job now, he would be satisfied. But she resolutely advocated that since things are going so smoothly, a good opportunity should not be missed. Simply try to get some real power and become a higher-level officer in charge of troops. At the very least, you should get a colonel's regiment leader of the infantry. Even if there is no ready-made vacancy to fill, you can still request to establish a new team and recruit troops yourself. I have already told Old Ye that you have such reputation and strength in this hometown. Whether it is to recruit bandits or incorporate militia, you can immediately call for many people. Just ask Old Ye to issue a commission and give you the title of a brigade commander or commander. I guarantee that you can exert effort and repay Old Ye. When An Yutian heard this, he was shocked and jumped up, waving his hands and said, "You are saying things too flamboyantly and without limit. Although it is said that in today's world, one should not be too honest, you still have to exaggerate a little. But I absolutely do not have such great ability to brag and exaggerate like you. After bragging, how can I manage to do it in the future? Wouldn't it eventually become a joke?"

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Commentary

The Ghost in the Tall House in England 248

— Fu Fo

The question of whether ghosts and gods exist has been debated in our country for thousands of years and has not yet been resolved. Now, strangely, it has happened in England, the world of science.

According to Reuters, in Liverpool, England, a large house has been haunted in recent years. Men are pushed down the stairs by ghosts, and women are thrown into the hall by ghosts, causing the neighbors to be terrified. It is truly strange. Confucius did not talk about ghosts, forces, and chaos, and did not dare to say there were no ghosts, but simply did not talk about them. He also said to respect ghosts and gods and keep them at a distance. If there are no ghosts and gods, why respect them? It seems that Confucius still advocated dualism. During the Six Dynasties, Xiao Ziliang was devoted to Buddhism, and Fan Zhen strongly argued that there was no Buddha. Zhen also wrote a theory of destroying gods, believing that form is the substance of the spirit, and the spirit is the function of form. The relationship between the spirit and form is like the sharpness of a knife. It has never been heard that the sharpness survives when the knife is gone. Ziliang could not refute him. Fan Zhen absolutely advocated monism.

However, according to what I have heard, there are countless strange books in our country. Even the facts heard and seen from friends cannot be exhausted. Therefore, I take the essence and use it widely, to scare Bo You. It is not impossible to speculate with common sense. Even Dr. Wu Tingfang had the theory of communication between humans and ghosts. A certain British spiritualist also said that there are five ghosts that can be talked to directly.

Recently, "scientists" and "metaphysicians" have been arguing with each other, incompatible with each other. I think it is because science has not been fully developed. If the study of the soul is researched using scientific methods, it will definitely be possible to successfully create a specialized field of learning.

Since then, more than ten years of fleeting time, the local area has been clean and peaceful.
